   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of countries by unemployment rate</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Wikipedia list article
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_(ILO).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_%28ILO%29.svg/400px-Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_%28ILO%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_%28ILO%29.svg/600px-Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_%28ILO%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_%28ILO%29.svg/800px-Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_%28ILO%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Unemployment_rate_map_of_the_world_(ILO).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Unemployment rate per country in 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>This is a <b>list of countries by unemployment rate</b>. Methods of calculation and presentation of <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> vary from country to country. Some countries count insured unemployed only, some count those in receipt of welfare benefit only, some count the disabled and other permanently unemployable people, some countries count those who choose (and are financially able) not to work, supported by their spouses and caring for a family, some count students at college and so on. There may also be differences in the minimum requirements and some consider people employed even if only marginally associated with employment market (for example, working only one hour per week).<sup id="cite_ref-Gallup-Unemployment_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallup-Unemployment-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There can be differences in the age limit. For example, <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> uses 15 to 74 years old when calculating unemployment rate, and the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Labor_Statistics" title="Bureau of Labor Statistics">Bureau of Labor Statistics</a> uses anyone 16 years of age or older (in both cases, people who are under education, retired, on maternity/paternity leave, prevented from working due to health, or do not work but have been inactive in seeking employment in the last four weeks are excluded from the <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a>, and therefore not counted as unemployed).<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat-unem_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-unem-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BLS-how_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BLS-how-3">[3]</a></sup> Unemployment rates are often <a href="/wiki/Seasonally_adjusted" class="mw-redirect" title="Seasonally adjusted">seasonally adjusted</a> to avoid variations that depend on time of year.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat-unem_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-unem-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BLS-how_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BLS-how-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_employment_rate" title="List of countries by employment rate">Employment rate as a percentage of total population in working age</a> is sometimes used instead of unemployment rate. </p>
      <p>For purposes of comparison, harmonized values are published by <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> (ILO) and by <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SL.UEM.TOTL.ZS">ILO harmonized unemployment rate</a> refers to those who are currently not working but are willing and able to work for pay, currently available to work, and have actively searched for work. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://data.oecd.org/unemp/unemployment-rate.htm#indicator-chart">OECD harmonized unemployment rate</a> gives the number of unemployed persons as a percentage of the labour force. Most unemployment rates given in the table below are derived from national statistics and therefore not directly comparable. </p>
